            <tr class='athing comtr' id='30713029'><td><table border='0'>  <tr>    <td class='ind'indent='0'><img src="s.gif" height="1" width="0"></td><td valign="top" class="votelinks">
      <center><a id='up_30713029' class='clicky' href='vote?id=30713029&amp;how=up&amp;auth=b600e06498647a2bd7b1b67c3167695ba83b8303&amp;goto=item%3Fid%3D30712175#30713029'><div class='votearrow' title='upvote'></div></a></center>    </td><td class="default"><div style="margin-top:2px; margin-bottom:-10px;"><span class="comhead">
          <a href="user?id=aghilmort" class="hnuser">aghilmort</a> <span class="age" title="2022-03-17T16:34:14"><a href="item?id=30713029">12 hours ago</a></span> <span id="unv_30713029"></span><span class="navs"> | <a href="#30715496" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">prev</a> | <a href="#30712576" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">next</a></span> <a class="togg clicky" id="30713029" n="1" href="javascript:void(0)">[–]</a><span class="onstory"></span>                  </span></div><br><div class="comment">
                  <span class="commtext c00">depends on function for me:<p>- new features tend to be one clean PR since there&#x27;s so much experimentation on what will work and lots of commits tends to slow things down -- a nominal disk backup is helpful, or even just a commit when taking a break on a branch of your own, no PRs until clean<p>- refactoring tends to be lots of test &#x2F; experimental &#x2F; ugly branches with incremental PRs, since tends to be easier to say, ok, change this one thing<p>- been experimenting with some third in-between mode, say add X with a bit more of a planning &#x2F; sprint mindset vs. oh wow, let&#x27;s see if this works<p>- feels like this approach is more of works for startups, probably harder to do in enterprise &#x2F; large teams?</span>

            <tr class='athing comtr' id='30713470'><td><table border='0'>  <tr>    <td class='ind'indent='0'><img src="s.gif" height="1" width="0"></td><td valign="top" class="votelinks">
      <center><a id='up_30713470' class='clicky' href='vote?id=30713470&amp;how=up&amp;auth=836475828f222fde17fa8ed57d33f253b9a11e89&amp;goto=item%3Fid%3D30712175#30713470'><div class='votearrow' title='upvote'></div></a></center>    </td><td class="default"><div style="margin-top:2px; margin-bottom:-10px;"><span class="comhead">
          <a href="user?id=throwawayboise" class="hnuser">throwawayboise</a> <span class="age" title="2022-03-17T17:12:34"><a href="item?id=30713470">11 hours ago</a></span> <span id="unv_30713470"></span><span class="navs"> | <a href="#30713624" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">prev</a> | <a href="#30716464" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">next</a></span> <a class="togg clicky" id="30713470" n="1" href="javascript:void(0)">[–]</a><span class="onstory"></span>                  </span></div><br><div class="comment">
                  <span class="commtext c00">All I use in git is clone, pull, commit, push. I do not use feature branches. The only branches I use are for releases that need to be maintained separately from master.<p>I absolutely do not care if there are &quot;fix typo&quot; or WIP commits in the history. The amount of effort it takes to get a &quot;clean&quot; commit history has negative payback in my experience.<p>It should be said I am a lone developer for the most part, sometimes working with one or two other people. So Git in fact is overkill for that scenario. Subversion would do just as well and in fact I prefer it or mercurial.<p>In a large project such as Git is meant for, my usage probably doesn&#x27;t apply.</span>

            <tr class='athing comtr' id='30714583'><td><table border='0'>  <tr>    <td class='ind'indent='0'><img src="s.gif" height="1" width="0"></td><td valign="top" class="votelinks">
      <center><a id='up_30714583' class='clicky' href='vote?id=30714583&amp;how=up&amp;auth=95774b177147e9b7413820f5b96865495b39f83c&amp;goto=item%3Fid%3D30712175#30714583'><div class='votearrow' title='upvote'></div></a></center>    </td><td class="default"><div style="margin-top:2px; margin-bottom:-10px;"><span class="comhead">
          <a href="user?id=aurelianito" class="hnuser">aurelianito</a> <span class="age" title="2022-03-17T18:51:31"><a href="item?id=30714583">10 hours ago</a></span> <span id="unv_30714583"></span><span class="navs"> | <a href="#30715200" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">prev</a> | <a href="#30713834" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">next</a></span> <a class="togg clicky" id="30714583" n="1" href="javascript:void(0)">[–]</a><span class="onstory"></span>                  </span></div><br><div class="comment">
                  <span class="commtext c00">Commit early. But do not commit garbage. Each commit should be a small but meaningful advance. All tests should pass. If working with compiled code, off course it should compile. No todos. No clunky var or method names. A branch per merge request.<p>If you do it like this it is great for everyone. Do not squash commits or rebase. Those are antipatterns. We are lying to ourselves when we do it. We cannot learn from history we rewrite.</span>
              <div class='reply'>        <p><font size="1">
                      <u><a href="reply?id=30714583&amp;goto=item%3Fid%3D30712175%2330714583">reply</a></u>

            <tr class='athing comtr' id='30713834'><td><table border='0'>  <tr>    <td class='ind'indent='0'><img src="s.gif" height="1" width="0"></td><td valign="top" class="votelinks">
      <center><a id='up_30713834' class='clicky' href='vote?id=30713834&amp;how=up&amp;auth=16df28fcf6588cd1ee8620cf963db56114de4237&amp;goto=item%3Fid%3D30712175#30713834'><div class='votearrow' title='upvote'></div></a></center>    </td><td class="default"><div style="margin-top:2px; margin-bottom:-10px;"><span class="comhead">
          <a href="user?id=globular-toast" class="hnuser">globular-toast</a> <span class="age" title="2022-03-17T17:41:42"><a href="item?id=30713834">11 hours ago</a></span> <span id="unv_30713834"></span><span class="navs"> | <a href="#30714583" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">prev</a> | <a href="#30713326" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">next</a></span> <a class="togg clicky" id="30713834" n="1" href="javascript:void(0)">[–]</a><span class="onstory"></span>                  </span></div><br><div class="comment">
                  <span class="commtext c00">Rebase is the key.<p>There are two types of commit: checkpoints and versions.<p>Checkpoints are just you randomly deciding to &quot;save&quot; your progress. They don&#x27;t necessarily correspond to completely working versions. The commit messages can be completely inappropriate for sharing but only make sense to you.<p>Versions are fully working copies of the program that could be checked out, run, released etc. These are what you present to your team and what gets merged in the end.<p>Sometimes you can write a new version straight away but other times you&#x27;ll generate checkpoints first. Then you use rebase to get to versions. Use rebase as a way to make it look you are a superhuman writing perfect commits first time.<p>Getting good at rebasing takes some practice and pretty good understanding of git&#x27;s data model. Learn this. And learn how to use --fixup, --squash and --autosquash to make your life easier.</span>
              <div class='reply'>        <p><font size="1">
                      <u><a href="reply?id=30713834&amp;goto=item%3Fid%3D30712175%2330713834">reply</a></u>
                  </font>
      </div></div></td></tr>

      <center><a id='up_30712787' class='clicky' href='vote?id=30712787&amp;how=up&amp;auth=4bdc57bb26cb2fdaf3913d81d9d777819e5c3321&amp;goto=item%3Fid%3D30712175#30712787'><div class='votearrow' title='upvote'></div></a></center>    </td><td class="default"><div style="margin-top:2px; margin-bottom:-10px;"><span class="comhead">
          <a href="user?id=El_RIDO" class="hnuser">El_RIDO</a> <span class="age" title="2022-03-17T16:16:28"><a href="item?id=30712787">12 hours ago</a></span> <span id="unv_30712787"></span><span class="navs"> | <a href="#30712440" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">parent</a> | <a href="#30714735" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">prev</a> | <a href="#30712975" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">next</a></span> <a class="togg clicky" id="30712787" n="1" href="javascript:void(0)">[–]</a><span class="onstory"></span>                  </span></div><br><div class="comment">
                  <span class="commtext c00">This is a good example of how scale can bias your view! :-D<p>Personally I share the same experience: In the 30 years I&#x27;ve been using personal computers at home and work, only 2 disks failed on me, one was an error on my part during an OS upgrade and the second was an external disk that physically fell off my bed while I had it plugged into my notebook. So both of these weren&#x27;t really those random failures.<p>On the other hand, while working in an IT infra team of a 60 developer company with 4 racks full of servers for 3 years, we&#x27;d get to see about one failed SSD per 2 months and 2-3 failed disks or SSDs per year in servers.<p>During the 1 year I worked for the IT infra team at a smaller hospital of a medium sized city with a large VDI environment and two HP EVAs in a two datacenter configuration each, we&#x27;d get 3-4 disk failures per week. Those had over 140 disk per storage each and were approaching the end of their support life, being around 5 years old, so the failure ratio started to get higher.</span>

            <tr class='athing comtr' id='30712975'><td><table border='0'>  <tr>    <td class='ind'indent='1'><img src="s.gif" height="1" width="40"></td><td valign="top" class="votelinks">
      <center><a id='up_30712975' class='clicky' href='vote?id=30712975&amp;how=up&amp;auth=94c25e3c884012056b82330684da4d415a111faa&amp;goto=item%3Fid%3D30712175#30712975'><div class='votearrow' title='upvote'></div></a></center>    </td><td class="default"><div style="margin-top:2px; margin-bottom:-10px;"><span class="comhead">
          <a href="user?id=amarshall" class="hnuser">amarshall</a> <span class="age" title="2022-03-17T16:29:55"><a href="item?id=30712975">12 hours ago</a></span> <span id="unv_30712975"></span><span class="navs"> | <a href="#30712440" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">parent</a> | <a href="#30712787" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">prev</a> | <a href="#30715190" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">next</a></span> <a class="togg clicky" id="30712975" n="1" href="javascript:void(0)">[–]</a><span class="onstory"></span>                  </span></div><br><div class="comment">
                  <span class="commtext c00">Sure, but your anecdote does not refute in any way that they can fail. It’s all about risk vs. overhead of avoiding that risk. The overhead of pushing often is very low, so even with the low probability of a drive failure, there’s not much reason to not do so (or any other form of backup, really).</span>
              <div class='reply'>        <p><font size="1">
                      <u><a href="reply?id=30712975&amp;goto=item%3Fid%3D30712175%2330712975">reply</a></u>
                  </font>
      </div></div></td></tr>
        </table></td></tr>
            <tr class='athing comtr' id='30715190'><td><table border='0'>  <tr>    <td class='ind'indent='1'><img src="s.gif" height="1" width="40"></td><td valign="top" class="votelinks">
      <center><a id='up_30715190' class='clicky' href='vote?id=30715190&amp;how=up&amp;auth=d6634d0e725040d374a00c388819c98f9e3d1095&amp;goto=item%3Fid%3D30712175#30715190'><div class='votearrow' title='upvote'></div></a></center>    </td><td class="default"><div style="margin-top:2px; margin-bottom:-10px;"><span class="comhead">
          <a href="user?id=contingencies" class="hnuser">contingencies</a> <span class="age" title="2022-03-17T19:50:51"><a href="item?id=30715190">9 hours ago</a></span> <span id="unv_30715190"></span><span class="navs"> | <a href="#30712440" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">parent</a> | <a href="#30712975" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">prev</a> | <a href="#30712732" class="clicky" aria-hidden="true">next</a></span> <a class="togg clicky" id="30715190" n="1" href="javascript:void(0)">[–]</a><span class="onstory"></span>                  </span></div><br><div class="comment">
                  <span class="commtext c00">Some non physical failure scenarios I have experienced include catastrophic filesystem failures (NTFS: <i>never again</i>), loss of machine and no handy backup machine capable of reading the disk or filesystem in question (ext<i>X</i>, ZFS, etc.), accidental damage to disk, partition or filesystem tree due to bad code (operator error; PEBSAC).</span>
              <div class='reply'>        <p><font size="1">
                      <u><a href="reply?id=30715190&amp;goto=item%3Fid%3D30712175%2330715190">reply</a></u>
                  </font>
      </div></div></td></tr>
